67-original. **E2E fixture catalog reference document (`e2e/FIXTURES.md`).** Surfaced 2026-05-09 during Sprint 43 Phase A audit via Pattern 7 fixture-class enumeration. Six fixture extensions across Sprints 37/38/40/41/43 with no central reference: signed `CarrierAgreement` (Sprint 37), carrier `mcNumber` rotation (Sprint 38), `blocked-carrier@srl.invalid` (Sprint 40), compliance override cleanup (Sprint 41), waterfall + loadbid + shipper-portal fixtures (Sprint 43). Each sprint re-derives idempotency, naming convention (`*@srl.invalid` for test users, `E2E-*-FIXTURE` for commodity tags), `E2E_FIXTURES=true` gate, override-cleanup pattern. **Sprint shape:** create `e2e/FIXTURES.md` documenting the gate, idempotency requirements (upsert + deleteMany before recreate when test mutates state), naming convention, current fixture inventory + ownership (which sprint added what). **Pairs with Item 64 (skill expansion)** as documentation-debt class. Prevents per-sprint re-derivation. ~50-100 LOC docs commit. Sprint 44+ candidate. **FIFTH consecutive sprint** where Pattern 7 enumeration surfaced multi-surface methodology debt — pattern is producing reliable signal, worth confirming "always-fire" status at next quarterly §19 review.

70. **Neon Launch tier — recurring cost + monitoring concern.** Surfaced 2026-05-09 during Sprint 44b Phase 1 (PITR upgrade pre-baseline-reset). PITR was raised from default to 7-day window before clearing the `_prisma_migrations` ledger + applying the new baseline migration. The 7-day PITR window is a Launch-tier feature — recurring monthly cost increase. **Sprint shape:** confirm Neon billing tier change is intentional (PITR safety vs cost trade-off). Decide canonical retention window post-Sprint-44b — keep at 7 days for ongoing safety on schema operations, or downgrade after a verification window. Document the chosen tier + rationale in CLAUDE.md §2 alongside the existing Neon connection note. Add billing review to monthly cost-monitoring cadence if not already there. **Priority:** low — operational, not blocking. Sprint 45+ candidate. Pairs with Item 64 (skill expansion) only loosely; primarily an infrastructure-hygiene item.

71. ~~**`(npx tsc || true)` suppresses TypeScript errors in build chain.**~~ **LOGGED + CLOSED 2026-05-10 in v3.8.abe** (Sprint 46). Root cause hypothesis from Sprint 44b Phase 3 was partially correct (the `|| true` did mask tsc errors) but Phase A audit at Sprint 46 revealed the deeper architectural cause: Render's env-level `NODE_ENV=production` (set in `render.yaml:34`) makes `npm install` skip the `devDependencies` block, leaving 12 declared `@types/*` packages uninstalled at build time. `Request` from `express` then resolves to `any`, `AuthRequest extends Request<any,any,any,any>` cascades, and tsc emits ~1,100 errors silenced by the `\|\| true`. Local CI uses `npm ci` (installs both deps + devDeps regardless of `NODE_ENV`) so CI tsc is clean — only Render diverged. **Empirical reproduction (Sprint 46 Phase B0 local sub-rule c gate):** `cd backend && rm -rf node_modules && NODE_ENV=production npm install && npm run build` produced exit code 0 with **1,398 error lines** (149 TS7016 + 907 TS2339 AuthRequest cascade + 63 TS7006 implicit any + 3 TS2503 Express namespace not found). Exact match to Sprint 45-RC Render build log. **Fix (3 changes, atomic):** (a) drop `\|\| true` from `backend/package.json:7` build script — strict tsc; (b) add `optionalDependencies` block with `@aws-sdk/client-rekognition ^3.1045.0` (Item 95, since we're touching package.json — biometricVerificationService.ts:9 has a try/catch dynamic require and was relying on the runtime-fail-graceful path); (c) add `NODE_ENV=development` prefix to Render dashboard buildCommand's `npm install` step — install-time only, runtime `NODE_ENV=production` preserved via render.yaml env block. **Architectural win:** build chain converted from fail-silent to fail-fast — tsc error → build halts → cp steps don't execute → deploy fails visibly. Sprint 45-RC's compass placeholder + Sprint 44b email signature fallback both shipped under fail-silent regime; Sprint 46 makes the next class of these visible in build logs immediately. **Sub-rule c lineage extends to 12 fires** in cumulative session arc (Sprint 46 audit-then-Phase-B0-gate counts as fire #11; fire #12 is the post-fix verification that landed clean). Per §3.1: v3.8.abd → v3.8.abe. **Items 95 + 96 closed alongside.**

95. ~~**`@aws-sdk/client-rekognition` referenced via dynamic require but not declared in package.json.**~~ **LOGGED + CLOSED 2026-05-10 in v3.8.abe** (Sprint 46 bundled with Item 71). [`backend/src/services/biometricVerificationService.ts:5-17`](backend/src/services/biometricVerificationService.ts#L5) wraps `require("@aws-sdk/client-rekognition")` in a try/catch gated by `AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID` env. The runtime warning `[Biometric] AWS Rekognition SDK not available, using hash-based verification` is the intentional fallback path. But the module was referenced without being declared anywhere in `package.json` (not in `dependencies`, `devDependencies`, or `optionalDependencies`) — meaning even if `AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID` were set, the require would still fail because npm never installed the package. Sprint 46 added `optionalDependencies` block: `{ "@aws-sdk/client-rekognition": "^3.1045.0" }`. Aligns with sibling `@aws-sdk/client-s3 ^3.998.0` major version. npm will try to install but won't fail if not available (graceful degradation matches the try/catch shape). When Wasi enables AWS biometric verification (set `AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID` env), Rekognition path will actually be reachable. **Surfaced during Sprint 46 Phase A4 audit** — we were already touching package.json, so bundled atomically per §3.3.

99. ~~**`cp -r` POSIX nesting bug + sub-rule c gate extension (file-landed-at-expected-path verification).**~~ **LOGGED + CLOSED 2026-05-16 in v3.8.abf** (Sprint 47 atomic Item 99). Linux/POSIX `cp -r SRC DEST` semantics: when DEST already exists as a directory, SRC is copied as a CHILD of DEST → result `DEST/SRC_NAME/files...`. Only when DEST does not exist does cp create it with SRC's contents flat. `tsc` creates `dist/backend/src/{lib,config,assets}/` directories first (emitting compiled `.js` files into them), so by the time the buildCommand's cp steps run, all three destinations pre-exist → nesting fires silently. **Two retroactive production regressions explained:** (a) Sprint 44b Item 72 logged + closed `cp -r src/config dist/backend/src/config` step, but the file actually landed at `dist/backend/src/config/config/signatures/whaider.html` (nested). [`email/builder.ts:18`](backend/src/email/builder.ts#L18) reading `dist/backend/src/config/signatures/whaider.html` got "file not found" warning on every cold start since Sprint 44b. (b) Sprint 45-RC compass mark PNGs went to `dist/backend/src/lib/lib/srl_compass_*.png` (nested). Runtime `LOGO_DIR = __dirname` resolved to `dist/backend/src/lib/`, `resolveCompassPng()` returned null, placeholder navy ring fired on every Rate Confirmation PDF. Same single bug class, two visible failures. **Fix:** trailing-dot form `cp -r SRC/. DEST/` always copies CONTENTS regardless of whether DEST exists. Applied to all 3 cp commands in render.yaml + CLAUDE.md §2.2. **Empirical verification (Sprint 47 Phase B0 sub-rule c gate):** reproduced nesting locally + verified trailing-dot fix produces flat paths before commit. **Methodology principle banked (Item 99):** for file-producing build operations, "command exited 0" is necessary but NOT sufficient verification — must also verify file landed at expected runtime path. Sprint 44b Item 72 closure was technically incorrect: the cp command did run with exit 0, but the runtime path was never checked; the failure was invisible until Sprint 45-RC compass placeholder surfaced it 6+ days later. Sub-rule c gate extends: command-success verification + file-path verification. Pattern 6 sub-rule c fire #13 banks the extended gate for future build-chain sprints.

100. ~~**Skill canonical transit display unit — days → hours (broker industry standard drive-hour metric).**~~ **LOGGED + CLOSED 2026-05-16 in v3.8.abf** (Sprint 47 atomic Item 100). Sprint 45-RC's `drawLaneEconomics` rendered transit as `${transitDays.toFixed(1)} days` (hardcoded). Pre-Sprint-47 RC PDF for 1,352-mile lane showed "2.7 days" (from `miles / 500` solo HOS pacing). Technically correct math but UX-poor — carriers convert mentally to drive hours regardless because HOS log entries, ETA windows, and dispatch conversations all run in hours. Per broker industry survey (TQL/Convoy/Uber Freight rate cons reviewed during Sprint 47 Phase A): every major broker's lane economics widget uses hours, not days. **Fix:** added optional `transitUnit: "hours" | "days" = "hours"` parameter to `drawLaneEconomics` in [`backend/src/lib/srl-chrome.ts`](backend/src/lib/srl-chrome.ts) (default "hours" per Sprint 47 D3); RC generator in [`pdfService.ts`](backend/src/services/pdfService.ts) now computes `transitHours = miles / 55` (industry-standard 55 mph highway average) and passes `"hours"`. Display: "24.6 hrs" for the same 1,352-mile lane. **Days path preserved** for any future caller that wants calendar-day display (multi-day plan, HOS-strict pacing). Skill `srl_chrome.ts` upstream sync recommended at next skill update — current change is local-only mirror of skill canonical.

101. ~~**Skill font registration in `srl-chrome.ts` mirroring BOL v2.9 pattern.**~~ **LOGGED + CLOSED 2026-05-16 in v3.8.abf** (Sprint 47 atomic Item 101). Sprint 45-RC's RC PDF rendered in Helvetica + Times-Bold (PDFKit built-ins), diverging from BOL v2.9's Playfair Display + DM Sans (skill canonical per `tokens.md`). User-visible inconsistency: BOL and RC are sibling shipping documents but used different font stacks. **Root cause:** `backend/src/lib/srl-chrome.ts:76-81` hardcoded PDFKit built-in font names (`Helvetica`, `Times-Bold`, etc.) for portability — the skill chrome was authored to work without registering custom TTFs. But in this monorepo, TTFs already ship at `backend/src/assets/fonts/bol-v2.9/` (9 files: 4 Playfair + 5 DMSans variants) from the Sprint v3.8.b BOL v2.9 epic. **Fix:** (a) updated FONT_* constants to skill canonical names (`Playfair-Bold`, `DMSans-Regular`, etc.); (b) added exported `registerSkillFonts(doc)` function mirroring `generateBOLFromLoad` registration pattern at `pdfService.ts:317-326`; (c) RC generator in `generateEnhancedRateConfirmation` now invokes `registerSkillFonts(doc)` immediately after `new PDFDocument(...)`. Without the registration call, fontkit throws "Font not found" on first text() invocation. **Courier-Bold preserved** (PDFKit built-in mono — skill spec doesn't include a custom monospace; kept for reference fields like load IDs + TRACK label per `pdf-chrome.md`). **Ligature suppression** — Sprint v3.8.b Option β monkey-patch at `pdfService.ts:197-265` prevents fontkit ligature substitution (`classified → classifed` bug). If RC PDF renders italic Playfair with ligature artifacts post-Sprint-47, same monkey-patch approach migrates into `srl-chrome.ts` as a separate hotfix; deferred unless surfaces visually.

103. ~~**Fontkit ligature substitution bug — "Rate Confirmation" rendered as "Rate Confrmation" post-Sprint-47.**~~ **LOGGED + CLOSED 2026-05-16 in v3.8.abg** (Sprint 47.b atomic Item 103). Sprint 47 visual verification post-deploy surfaced the bug exactly as the Sprint 47 commit message predicted ("deferred unless surfaces visually"). 3 of 4 "Rate Confirmation" instances rendered with the `fi` glyph substitution that truncates the `i` — affecting Playfair-Bold 22pt H1 display, DMSans-Regular 8pt continuation header, and DMSans-Italic 7.5pt CARRIER · ACCEPTANCE body. Only the legacy Helvetica T&C body rendered correctly because PDFKit built-in fonts have no fontkit ligature substitution. **Root cause:** same fontkit `liga`/`clig`/`rlig`/`dlig` OpenType feature substitution Sprint v3.8.b Option β monkey-patch fixed for BOL v2.9 (classified → classifed bug). Sprint 47 added skill canonical font registration (`registerSkillFonts(doc)`) but didn't port the monkey-patch — explicitly documented as "deferred unless surfaces visually" in Sprint 47 commit. **Fix:** ported the canonical monkey-patch verbatim from [`pdfService.ts:248-297`](backend/src/services/pdfService.ts#L248) into the END of `registerSkillFonts(doc)` in [`backend/src/lib/srl-chrome.ts:119+`](backend/src/lib/srl-chrome.ts#L119). Bundled with font registration — every skill-chrome consumer that calls `registerSkillFonts(doc)` now inherits BOTH font registration AND ligature suppression in one call. Future Sprint 45-RC2 (Invoice) + 45-RC3 (Settlement) migrations auto-benefit. Monkey-patch disables 4 OpenType ligature features (`liga`/`clig`/`rlig`/`dlig`) while preserving `kern: true` for proper typography. Exact-shape verbatim port verified Phase B0 sub-rule c gate. **Phase B1 sub-rule c gate D4:** local PDF smoke test generated post-fix RC PDF via direct service call; pdf-parse text extraction verified all 4 "Rate Confirmation" instances render with the dot on `i`. Empirical proof BEFORE commit + push. Net source change: ~50 LOC in `srl-chrome.ts`. CLOSED in Sprint 47.b.

104. ~~**T&C body + 3 coupled Helvetica references in `generateEnhancedRateConfirmation` swapped to FONT_BODY/FONT_BODY_BOLD skill canonical.**~~ **LOGGED + CLOSED 2026-05-16 in v3.8.abg** (Sprint 47.b atomic Item 104 bundled with Item 103). Original directive scope was T&C body (1 line: `doc.font("Helvetica", 7.5)` at line 1567). Scope EXPANDED to 4 Helvetica references during Phase B0 audit because (a) `heightOfString(text)` measurement at line 1526 must use the same font as text rendering at line 1540 to produce a correctly-sized panel — coupled pair must migrate together; (b) T&C section label at line 1549 (`Helvetica-Bold 7pt`) paired with body at line 1567 for visual consistency — splitting them would render T&C header in Helvetica-Bold and body in DMSans, introducing a NEW visual inconsistency worse than Sprint 47 baseline; (c) all 4 references are in the same generator function + same atomic commit per §3.3. Plus added `export` keyword to `FONT_BODY` + `FONT_BODY_BOLD` constants in srl-chrome.ts (were `const` before, not exported); imported in pdfService.ts. **Safe post-Item-103 monkey-patch** — DMSans fonts are precisely the fonts that exhibited the ligature substitution bug Item 103 fixed; without the monkey-patch port, Item 104's swap would have introduced new ligature artifacts on the previously-clean Helvetica T&C body. Items 103 + 104 must ship atomically; deploying 104 without 103 would be a regression. Net source change: ~6 LOC in pdfService.ts (4 font calls + 2 lines added to import block) + ~6 LOC in srl-chrome.ts (export keywords on 6 FONT_* constants). CLOSED in Sprint 47.b.

105. ~~**Pattern 6 sub-rule c — "deferred-but-not-missed" protocol canonical (named sub-pattern).**~~ **LOGGED + CLOSED 2026-05-16 in v3.8.abg** (Sprint 47.b methodology meta-finding). Sprint 47's commit message explicitly documented the deferred ligature risk verbatim: *"Ligature suppression — Sprint v3.8.b Option β monkey-patch... if RC PDF renders italic Playfair with ligature artifacts post-Sprint-47, same monkey-patch approach migrates into srl-chrome.ts as a separate hotfix; deferred unless surfaces visually."* When the risk surfaced via Wasi's visual verification of the post-Sprint-47 RC PDF, Sprint 47.b activated exactly per that documented plan — single-day turnaround from surface → atomic fix → push. **This is NOT a sub-rule c miss.** Sprint 47 didn't have the data to know the ligature would visibly surface (could have been correctly rendered by Playfair's specific `fi` glyph; fontkit ligature behavior varies by font's OpenType tables). Documenting the deferred risk as a known-conditional follow-up sprint, with explicit activation criteria, is the gate's INTENDED deferral protocol. Sub-rule c fire count holds at 13 — deferred-but-not-missed is a sub-pattern, not a fire. **Methodology principle banked:** when a sprint identifies a downstream risk it can't empirically validate at commit time (e.g., visual rendering that needs production-equivalent deployment), document the risk + activation criteria + planned hotfix path in the commit message. Future sprints have a clear handoff if the risk materializes. The protocol works as designed when (a) Sprint N flags the risk explicitly, (b) Sprint N+1 activates immediately when verification surfaces it. §19 quarterly meta-commit candidate alongside Item 96 (fail-fast vs fail-silent) and Item 99 (runtime-path verification gate extension). Sub-rule c now has THREE named methodology principles: authoritative-source-verification (canonical), fail-fast-build-chain (Item 96), runtime-path-verification (Item 99), AND deferred-but-not-missed (Item 105). All four are §19 case studies for next quarterly review.

102. ~~**`drawPartiesBlock` y-coordinate overlap with meta strip date row.**~~ **LOGGED + CLOSED 2026-05-16 in v3.8.abf** (Sprint 47 atomic Item 102). Sprint 45-RC PDF rendered "May 16, 2026PARTIES" as visible overlap on page 1 — the meta strip's DATE value row collided with the `drawPartiesBlock` PARTIES small-caps label sitting `y - 14` above the panels. Root cause: in [`pdfService.ts:1414`](backend/src/services/pdfService.ts#L1414) the RC generator called `drawPartiesBlock(..., y - 4)`; `drawMetaStrip` returns y at meta strip's bottom edge, and `drawPartiesBlock` internally subtracts 14 from the passed `yTop` to position its PARTIES label, so the effective label y was `metaStripBottom - 4 - 14 = metaStripBottom - 18`, which fell INSIDE the meta strip's value row. **Fix:** bumped y-offset from `y - 4` to `y + 12` — gives the parties label clearance from the meta strip row above. Visually verified via local rebuild + Wasi pixel verification on Phase 4 post-deploy.

96. ~~**Architectural lesson — build chain fail-fast vs fail-silent as canonical methodology principle.**~~ **LOGGED + CLOSED 2026-05-10 in v3.8.abe** (Sprint 46 meta-finding). Pre-Sprint-46 backend build chain: `npm install (NODE_ENV=production skips devDeps) → (npx tsc \|\| true) (mask errors) → cp -r src/assets/config/lib (succeeds unconditionally) → prisma migrate deploy → deploy succeeds with broken artifacts`. Net effect: TWO classes of regression silently shipped to production over the past sprint arc — (1) Sprint 44b email signature template `dist/backend/src/config/signatures/whaider.html` missing (caught by Sprint 44b Item 72 pre-commit grep audit, fixed by adding `cp -r src/config` step — but the underlying fail-silent build chain wasn't addressed); (2) Sprint 45-RC compass mark PNGs `dist/backend/src/lib/srl_compass_*.png` missing despite buildCommand including `cp -r src/lib` step — the cp didn't fail, the `tsc` step "passed" (via `\|\| true`), so the deploy went through with broken assets; user saw placeholder navy ring instead of canonical SRL compass mark. **Post-Sprint-46 build chain is fail-fast:** tsc errors → npm run build exits non-zero → cp steps don't run → deploy halts with visible failure. Future Sprint-44b/45-RC class regressions become impossible at the architectural level rather than requiring per-incident pre-commit grep audits. **Methodology principle:** silent-success is worse than loud-failure on prod deploy chains because (a) silent-success normalizes ignoring the build log noise, (b) the failure mode propagates to runtime where it's harder to diagnose, (c) eventually shipping a "live" service that's missing assets damages user trust. Banking for §19 quarterly meta-commit as canonical methodology principle. **Item 96 LOG + CLOSE** — the principle is now documented at CLAUDE.md §2.2 + permanently embedded in the post-Sprint-46 build chain itself.

73. ~~**Sprint 44b initial directive specified `--exit-code` flag on `prisma migrate status` in build chain — flag absent in Prisma 6.x.**~~ **LOGGED + CLOSED 2026-05-09 in v3.8.aay** (Sprint 44b hotfix — regression caught via Render redeploy failure signal). Render production deploy fired the new canonical buildCommand and failed with `unknown or unexpected option: --exit-code` AFTER `prisma migrate deploy` ran clean ("No pending migrations to apply"). Authoritative-source check via `npx prisma migrate status --help` confirmed Prisma 6.19 exposes only `--help / --config / --schema`; the `--exit-code` flag was either renamed/removed in v6 transition or never existed there. **Gate behavior intact** — Prisma 6 returns non-zero exit code on drift inherently (verified via PowerShell `$LASTEXITCODE = 0` after clean `migrate status` run; drift produces non-zero). Hotfix drops the flag from §2.2 + render.yaml + Render dashboard. Item 73 closes same-sprint as caught. **Pattern 6 sub-rule c THIRD prospective fire in single Sprint 44b session** — directive's flag specification looked complete on the surface, but authoritative-source verification (Prisma `--help` output) revealed the flag's absence. Three-fire validation lineage canonicalizes sub-rule c at Sprint 44.5 (already promoted from candidate post-Phase-3 Item 72).

72. ~~**`cp -r src/config dist/backend/src/config` step dropped from Sprint 44b Render Build Command.**~~ **LOGGED + CLOSED 2026-05-09 in v3.8.aax** (Sprint 44b atomic close — regression averted pre-deploy). Pre-commit grep on `backend/src/` surfaced `backend/src/email/builder.ts:18` runtime-loading `__dirname`-relative path `../config/signatures/whaider.html` — load-bearing for production email signatures (Lead Hunter outreach + onboarding emails + every founder-from email per CLAUDE.md §3.10). Sprint 44b directive's draft buildCommand omitted the `cp -r src/config` step; first prod deploy after that draft would have broken Resend sends with missing-template errors. Pattern 6 sub-rule c (audits-can-be-wrong / verify prod-touching action against authoritative source before acting) fired prospectively in real-time during Sprint 44b — directive author didn't have Item 72's audit findings at directive time; pre-commit verification grep surfaced the gap before the commit landed. Resolution: `cp -r src/config dist/backend/src/config` restored to (a) Render dashboard buildCommand (Wasi pre-commit), (b) render.yaml (this commit), (c) CLAUDE.md §2.2 canonical (this commit). Net effect: zero deploy-time regression; Item 72 closes same-sprint as logged. **Methodology lesson:** the rule *"every commit that mutates the build chain triggers a `grep __dirname.*config\|src/assets/` audit before commit"* is now baked into §2.2's added note about `__dirname`-relative assets. Future build-command changes won't re-derive this risk surface.

74. ~~**Frontend POST tender URL drifted from Sprint 37f canonical (singular verb form).**~~ **LOGGED + CLOSED 2026-05-09 in v3.8.aaz** (Sprint 44c hotfix). Single-character delete. **Path α chosen** over Path β (which would have flipped backend + apiDocs + E2E + Sprint 37f comment to plural — broader blast radius, would reverse Sprint 37f intent). **Pattern 6 sub-rule c FOURTH prospective fire** — directive's "single-line fix line 14 (backend)" framing surfaced 9 hits across 4 files via Pattern 7 multi-surface grep; Sprint 37f intent caught + scope corrected before any code change. 76. **Methodology meta — Pattern 6 sub-rule c earned status post-Sprint-44b provides defense-in-depth even against directives issued by methodology-aware agents.** Surfaced 2026-05-09 during Sprint 44c hotfix Phase A. Sub-rule c was canonicalized at Sprint 44.5 with three-fire validation across Sprint 44b (Phase 1 ProspectVertical → 81 of 87 enums; Phase 3 cp src/config; Phase 4 --exit-code flag). Sprint 44c's directive came from the same methodology-aware author and STILL contained inferences that the authoritative source contradicted. Mechanism this time: a separate AI agent (Claude Sonnet running this session) ran multi-surface grep across `.{ts,tsx,js,jsx}` before accepting the directive's "single-line backend fix" framing — surfaced 9 hits across 4 files vs the directive's 2-file framing, caught Sprint 37f intent the directive missed entirely, surfaced E2E regression risk, presented Path α / Path β decision to user with full evidence. Methodology integrity check passed — sub-rule c protects against subsequent agents' (or directives') incomplete-audit inferences exactly as designed. **Sprint shape:** docs-only meta-commit candidate at next quarterly §19 review. Add to §19 Pattern 6 sub-rule c body as a fourth-fire validation example, or fold into Sprint 44.5-style methodology meta-commit. **Lesson worth banking:** sub-rule c is proven-defensive across at least four prospective fires within a 24-hour window across two sessions and two directive authors. Pattern is now demonstrably the most active §19 lens of the entire methodology library. Item 76 LOG OPEN; closure deferred until quarterly §19 review. **Updated by Sprint 44d (2026-05-09):** Item 79 supersedes this as the canonical retrospective tracker — five-fire validation including the Sprint 44d expiresAt-missing finding extends the lineage. Item 76 stays open as the four-fire snapshot; Item 79 is the live tracker.

77. **Broker-configurable tender expiry UX in the AE Tender modal.** Surfaced 2026-05-09 during Sprint 44d Path α decision. Currently `frontend/src/app/dashboard/loads/page.tsx:271` (post-Sprint-44d) sends `expiresAt: new Date(Date.now() + 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000).toISOString()` — a 24h-from-now broker-default that matches the E2E canonical at [`e2e/full-lifecycle.spec.ts:155`](e2e/full-lifecycle.spec.ts#L155) and industry convention for direct tendering. The Tender modal has no UI surface to set this — AE cannot tighten to a 4h window for an urgent load or extend to 48h for a flexible-window load. Backend [`tenders.ts:35`](backend/src/routes/tenders.ts#L35) already has `expirationMinutes: z.number().min(15).max(1440).default(60)` for the waterfall path (15min-24h range, 60min default) — direct-tender path inherits no equivalent control. **Sprint shape:** add expiry input to Tender modal at `loads/page.tsx` around the existing tenderRate input (~lines 1815-1820 area per Sprint 36 picker rewrite). Default value 24h, range 15min-72h with sensible presets (1h / 4h / 24h / 48h). Wire into createTender mutation body to override the hardcoded fallback. ~30-50 LOC. Pairs with the waterfall expirationMinutes input — could ship as a small consolidation sprint. **Sprint 46+ candidate.** Not BKN-blocking — 24h default is the broker-industry standard and matches what the platform shipped through Sprint 44d.

Per §3.1: v3.8.aam → v3.8.aan.

93. **Pattern 6 sub-rule c — pixel-verification-as-audit-gate observation.** Surfaced 2026-05-10 during Sprint 45-RC Phase A2 PDF capture. Phase A Track 1 audit produced 7 RC PDF findings via code-side analysis (read pdfService.ts, compared against skill canonical, traced data shapes). Phase A2 pixel verification (open the PDF, look at it) surfaced an 8th finding the code audit predicted nothing about: rate breakdown rendered to page 4 instead of page 1. The cause was `checkPageBreak` thresholds + section-ordering interaction that produced visible-but-non-obvious pagination behavior — invisible from grepping section names; visible only when looking at the rendered output. **Methodology lesson:** code-side audits are authoritative for code contracts (function signatures, type shapes, control flow) but NOT for visual contracts (which-page-does-X-render-on, what-does-the-rendered-pixel-density-feel-like, where-does-an-AE-eye-fall-first). Visual audits require visual capture — there's no shortcut via grep, AST parsing, or static type inspection. Code-side audit answers "what could it render?"; pixel verification answers "what does it render?". The two are complementary, not substitutable. **Sprint shape:** docs-only meta-commit candidate at next quarterly §19 review. Add to §19 Pattern 6 sub-rule c body as a NEW sub-class — pixel-verification-as-audit-gate distinct from authoritative-source-verification. Lineage: cumulative arc sub-rule c fire count post-Sprint-45-RC = 9, with Phase A2 (this finding) + Phase B Sub-phase 3 (package.json directive correction) being fires 8 + 9. **Item 93 LOG OPEN** — closure deferred until quarterly §19 review or Sprint 44.5-style methodology meta-commit appends the case-study addendum.

94. **`drawPanel` single-line `lineBreak: false` limitation surfaced during Sprint 45-RC RC migration.** Surfaced 2026-05-10 during Sprint 45-RC Phase B Sub-phase 2 implementation. Skill `srl-chrome.ts` `drawPanel` (line 667) renders `bodyText` with `lineBreak: false` — single-line only, no wrapping. For Rate Confirmation Special Instructions which can be multi-paragraph free-text, `drawPanel` is insufficient. **Workaround in Sprint 45-RC:** `generateEnhancedRateConfirmation` renders the cream-2 frame manually (using `doc.roundedRect.fillAndStroke`) + the body text with `width: CONTENT_W - 20, lineGap: 1` for proper wrapping. Same outcome visually as `drawPanel` would produce IF it supported wrapping. **Skill upstream fix:** `drawPanel` should accept a `wrap?: boolean` option (default false to preserve existing single-line callers) that switches `lineBreak: false` → text wrapping with measured panel height. ~10 LOC fix in `srl-chrome.ts`. When implemented, mirror the change into `backend/src/lib/srl-chrome.ts` (the per-skill manual-sync rule still applies). **Sprint shape:** skill-side fix at next skill update; backend mirror at next manual sync. Not BKN-blocking — Sprint 45-RC's manual workaround produces equivalent visual output today.

45. **RC Modal payload spread includes fields not declared in validator (`totalCarrierPay`, `netPayAmount`).** Surfaced 2026-05-06 during Sprint 34 Phase A. [`RateConfirmationModal.tsx`](frontend/src/components/loads/RateConfirmationModal.tsx) `buildPayload()` does `...form` spread which includes `totalCarrierPay` (FormState line 184) and `netPayAmount` (line 189). Backend validator [`createRateConfirmationSchema`](backend/src/validators/rateConfirmation.ts) does NOT declare these fields. Zod's default behavior is `.strip()` — unknown keys are silently dropped from the parsed output without raising validation errors. **No current bug** — fields are silently discarded server-side. **Cleanup options:** (a) remove from `...form` spread by reshaping payload to explicitly-listed fields only; (b) add the two fields to the validator schema if useful for backend (e.g., for analytics/audit); (c) change validator to `.strict()` to fail-loud on unknown keys. **Sprint shape:** small (~5 LOC) but architectural decision — option (a) is cleanest for forward compatibility, option (c) catches future drift but requires payload audit across all RC consumers. **NOT in Sprint 34 scope** per §3.3 atomic-commit rule — Sprint 34 stayed atomic on Item 42 closure. **Priority:** low. No load is currently broken. Pairs naturally with §13.3 Item A28-2 (validator hardening) post-BKN.

43. ~~**Silent error swallow on RC modal handlers — handleSaveDraft / handleGeneratePdf / handleSendTender catch blocks all `console.error` only with no UI feedback.**~~ **CLOSED 2026-05-06 in v3.8.aak** (Sprint 32 Path β). Bug class: "API failures invisible to user." Surfaced as a side-effect of Item 42 audit — even if Item 42 is fixed, future API failures on these handlers would silently fail the same way. Same defensive class as Sprint 26b error boundary patterns. **Fix:** added `submitError: string | null` state to RC modal root component; new `extractErrorMessage(err, fallback)` helper checks `err.response.data.error → .message → err.message → fallback` (handles axios + native Error + plain string shapes); all 3 handlers reset error to null at start, set error in catch block on failure; new JSX banner above button row conditionally rendered when `submitError` set — `bg-red-50 border-l-4 border-red-500 text-red-700` (canonical Tailwind error palette, works on cream + dark contexts) with "Error:" label prefix. Banner auto-dismisses on next handler attempt (resets at handler start). **Future API failures on these handlers self-diagnose via screenshot** — no DevTools workflow required. ~25 LOC (state + helper + 3 handler edits + JSX banner). **Pattern propagation candidate:** other modals/forms across the codebase likely have the same silent-error class; could roll up into a typing-discipline / observability sprint to apply pattern consistently. Not in Sprint 32 scope per §3.3 atomic-commit rule.

**RC Modal carrier search route fix — hotfix (logged + closed 2026-05-06 in v3.8.aaj, Sprint 31):**

39. ~~**RC Modal carrier search returns 404 silent-fail (B28-T1.3-A re-diagnosed).**~~ **CLOSED 2026-05-06 in v3.8.aaj** (Sprint 31). Originally walked as "P1 missing empty state on carrier search." Phase A audit corrected the diagnosis — the empty state was never the bug. Root cause: [`RateConfirmationModal.tsx:1422`](frontend/src/components/loads/RateConfirmationModal.tsx#L1422) (pre-fix) called `api.get("/carriers/all", ...)` but the canonical handler `getAllCarriers` is mounted at `/api/carrier/all` (singular) per [`backend/src/routes/carrier.ts:123`](backend/src/routes/carrier.ts#L123), NOT `/api/carriers/all` (plural). The plural route file defines `GET /` (with validation) and `GET /:id`, so Express matched `/api/carriers/all` against the `/:id` route with `req.params.id = "all"`, called `getCarrierDetail("all")` → returned 404. Frontend `useQuery` silently swallowed the 404, `data` stayed undefined, dropdown render gated on `showSearch && carriers && (...)` never fired — AE saw silent dead-state (input typed, no dropdown, no error, no autofill). **Re-diagnosis pattern matches Sprint 26 → 26b** (accessorial walk surfaced symptom, audit identified actual root cause): walk surfaces what user sees, audit identifies real bug class, correct fix ships. Memory #11 firing again. **Fix:** 1-character change — removed `s` from `carriers/all`. New URL `/carrier/all` now resolves to the actual `getAllCarriers` handler. Inline comment added at the call site referencing Sprint 31 + Item 40 (the duplicate-route consolidation backlog). **Pre-commit verification:** backend `tsc --noEmit` clean (no backend changes), frontend `next build` clean. Net LOC change: ~7 (1 URL char swap + 6-line inline comment). Per §3.1: v3.8.aai → v3.8.aaj.

40. **Duplicate carrier-route definitions: `routes/carrier.ts` (singular) vs `routes/carriers.ts` (plural).** Surfaced 2026-05-06 during Sprint 31 Phase A audit. Two backend files define routes for the same `getAllCarriers` controller at different URL paths with different validation: [`backend/src/routes/carrier.ts:123`](backend/src/routes/carrier.ts#L123) `GET /all` (NO validation, accepts arbitrary query params); [`backend/src/routes/carriers.ts:102`](backend/src/routes/carriers.ts#L102) `GET /` (WITH `validateQuery(carrierQuerySchema)`). Both call the same controller. Result: validation drift between `/api/carrier/all?search=X` (anything goes) and `/api/carriers?search=X` (must match Zod schema). Multiple frontend callers may hit either path. The plural route also defines `GET /:id` (`getCarrierDetail`) which is the silent-trap that caused Item 39's 404. **Sprint shape:** consolidate to one route file + one URL pattern. Recommend keeping the plural `/api/carriers` (REST convention for collection) with proper sub-paths: `GET /` (list), `GET /search` or `GET /?search=X` (search), `GET /:id` (detail). Migrate all frontend callers. Delete the singular file. Validation lives at the canonical path. **Effort:** medium — requires grep across `frontend/src/` for all `api.get("/carrier/...")` and `api.get("/carriers/...")` callers, decision on canonical paths, route file consolidation, then frontend updates. ~30-50 LOC across 5-10 files. **Out of Sprint 31 scope** per §3.3 "no scope creep" — Sprint 31 atomic on the silent-fail URL fix only. **Tracked for post-BKN architecture queue** per locked sprint sequencing.

**Production reliability — hotfix (logged + closed 2026-05-06 in v3.8.aah, Sprint 29):**

33. ~~**RateConfirmation modal accessorial shape mismatch — same root-cause class as Item 32 Load Board crash, different surface.**~~ **CLOSED 2026-05-06 in v3.8.aah** (Sprint 29 hotfix immediately after Sprint 28 Phase A surfaced it as A28-1 P0). Phase A static-analysis grep on `frontend/src/` for accessorial render sites surfaced [`RateConfirmationModal.tsx:418`](frontend/src/components/loads/RateConfirmationModal.tsx#L418) — pre-fix code: `description: a.description || a` fell through `|| a` to the whole `{type, amount, payer}` Order Builder object when `.description` was undefined. Object then propagated to (1) [`line 500`](frontend/src/components/loads/RateConfirmationModal.tsx#L500) `.filter((a) => a.description.trim())` → TypeError "a.description.trim is not a function"; (2) [`line 1716-1717`](frontend/src/components/loads/RateConfirmationModal.tsx#L1716) `<input value={acc.description} ... />` → React error #31 same as Sprint 26b. **Trigger conditions** identical to Item 32: load created via Order Builder convert flow + at least one accessorial added + AE opens RateConfirmation modal. **Fix** — defensive type-check pattern matching Sprint 26b. Three input shapes supported: string (legacy) → description = a; `{description, amount}` (RC's own saved shape from prior RC modal saves) → description = a.description; `{type, amount, payer}` (Order Builder shape per [`orders/types.ts:90`](frontend/src/app/dashboard/orders/types.ts#L90)) → description = a.type. Order Builder accessorial `{type: "Detention", amount: 0}` now hydrates as RC modal accessorial `{description: "Detention", amount: "0"}`. **Why Phase A caught it that Sprint 26b's frontend smoke didn't:** Sprint 26b smoke clicked Load Board side panel which doesn't open the RC modal — the RC modal is opened separately via "Send Rate Confirmation" action on a tendered load. The bug shape was identical but on a different render site. Sprint 28's static-analysis grep for accessorial readers surfaced this immediately, validating the audit-only sprint methodology. **Root-cause loophole still open (Sprint 31 candidate):** [`backend/src/validators/load.ts:113`](backend/src/validators/load.ts#L113) `accessorials: z.array(z.any()).optional()` accepts any shape — Sprint 26b + Sprint 29 both cosmetically patched consumer sides but Order Builder writes its shape and RC modal save writes its shape, so multiple shapes coexist in DB. Sprint 31 will tighten the validator + add data migration. Sprint 29 handles both shapes defensively at read time. **Pre-commit verification:** backend `tsc --noEmit` clean (no backend changes), frontend `next build` clean. Net LOC change: ~15 (1 file, accessorial hydrator block expanded from 1 line to ~17 with defensive type-check + comment block). Per §3.1 sequence-continuous rule: v3.8.aag → v3.8.aah. **Sprint 52 epic — tender workflow polish (banked §19 meta-50, 2026-05-16, post-Sprint-50 v3.8.abn session arc closure):**

141. **Tender expiry cron sweeper.** Logged 2026-05-16 §19 meta-50. Today `LoadTender.expiresAt` is enforced at validator write time (Sprint 44d Item 78) and surfaced in the RC PDF banner (Sprint 48 Item 108) but no background job sweeps past-expiry tenders. AE Console relies on the 30-second `refetchInterval` polling (Sprint 36 Item 50) to surface stale tenders, and the tender-decline email path (Sprint 45a `sendTenderExpiredEmail`, Item 80) has no firing trigger. **Sprint shape:** node-cron tick every 10 minutes that selects OFFERED tenders with `expiresAt < now`, flips status → EXPIRED, fires `notifyTenderAction(tender.id, "EXPIRED")`, advances any waterfall position to next-tier carrier where applicable. ~40 LOC across `backend/src/services/cronService.ts` (or new file) + tenderController helper. Sub-rule c gates: verify cron runtime (Render service supports cron via setInterval or external scheduler), authoritative-source check on EXPIRED status state machine downstream consumers. **Sprint 52a.** Not BKN-blocking — manual AE intervention works pre-cron; cron adds reliability + closes Item 80's defensive function reaching live state.

142. **Magic-link carrier accept-without-login.** Logged 2026-05-16 §19 meta-50. Today `sendTenderOfferedEmail` (Sprint 45a Item 80) lands in carrier inbox with a CTA pointing at `/carrier/dashboard/tenders` — carrier must log in to act. Industry-best brokers (CHR, Coyote, RXO, Convoy) all support magic-link accept/decline embedded in the tender email itself, removing the login friction class. **Sprint shape:** generate per-tender signed JWT (24h expiry) embedding `{tenderId, action: accept|decline}`; render two CTA buttons in `sendTenderOfferedEmail` ("Accept this load" / "Decline"); new public route `GET /api/tender-action/:token` verifies JWT, applies action, returns acknowledgment page (frontend route `/tender-action/[token]/page.tsx` or static HTML). Carriers can accept while driving / between loads / off-laptop. ~80-100 LOC across 4 files (token generator + email CTA + public endpoint + acknowledgment page). Sub-rule c gates: authoritative-source check on JWT lifecycle (matches existing `tracking` token pattern at Sprint 47.b Item 31 close), audit-both-ends-of-data-flow verify acknowledgment page can mutate tender status without auth context. **Sprint 52b.** Highest UX leverage item in tender workflow polish — drops tender acceptance latency from minutes to seconds.

143. **Counter-tender email handler.** Logged 2026-05-16 §19 meta-50. Originally banked as Item 89 (Sprint 45a) for Sprint 45b. Sprint 45b never materialized; counter-tender email path remains unfired. `notifyTenderAction("COUNTERED")` currently writes only the in-app `Notification` record; carrier-side counter-offer (currently no frontend UI to submit) and AE-side counter-receive (no email) both gaps. **Sprint shape:** (a) `sendTenderCounteredEmail` function in `emailService.ts` — AE-facing email when carrier counters; carrier-counter-offer requires frontend UI work which is Item 144 scope; (b) extend `notifyTenderAction` COUNTERED case to fire the email. ~25 LOC. **Sprint 52c.** Pairs with Items 142 + 144 — magic-link flow could embed counter UI inline.

144. **Tiered expiry preset UX (4h / 24h / 48h).** Logged 2026-05-16 §19 meta-50. Originally Item 77 (Sprint 44d) — AE Tender modal has no UI to set tender expiry; defaults to 24h hardcoded fallback. Industry pattern (TQL, Echo, Landstar) all expose expiry presets in the tender creation surface — 4-hour for urgent loads, 24-hour standard, 48-hour for flexible-window loads. Schema already supports custom `expiresAt` (Sprint 44d). **Sprint shape:** add 3-button preset toggle to Tender modal (`/dashboard/loads` page Tender form) + custom-expiry input fallback; wire into createTender mutation body to override the hardcoded 24h fallback. ~40 LOC. Sub-rule c gate: audit-both-ends-of-data-flow verify preset writes through validator (`expiresAt: z.string().transform(s => new Date(s))` already accepts arbitrary ISO strings, no validator change needed). **Sprint 52d.** Pairs with Sprint 45b ghost — closes the user's "optimal workflow" four-step spec retroactively.

87.b. **`LoadTender.declineReason` field + capture flow** (closes Item 87 schema gap; extends Item 90). Logged 2026-05-16 §19 meta-50. Today `LoadTender` schema has no `declineReason` field (Item 90 verification, Sprint 45a). `sendTenderDeclinedEmail` always passes `declineReason: undefined`; the conditional rendering (Sprint 45a D4) gracefully omits the row, but the AE-facing email reads "Tender declined by {carrier}" with no reason context. **Sprint shape:** (a) add `declineReason String?` to `LoadTender` schema migration, (b) extend `declineTender` controller to read `req.body.reason` (~5 LOC), (c) extend carrier portal `/carrier/dashboard/tenders` decline modal to capture reason — categorized dropdown (Rate too low / Capacity full / Lane mismatch / Equipment unavailable / Other) + free-text fallback, (d) magic-link decline flow (Item 142) inherits the reason capture via embedded JSON. ~80-120 LOC across 4 files + 1 migration. **Sprint 52e.** Item identifier `87.b` rather than 87 (Item 87 is the unrelated `emailTemplates.ts` wrapper consolidation). Pairs naturally with Items 142 + 143 — magic-link counter UI from Sprint 52b/c could embed decline-reason capture in the same flow.

145. **Engagement signals + decline taxonomy analytics.** Logged 2026-05-16 §19 meta-50. Post-Sprint-52a-d, the platform will have rich tender lifecycle data (offered → opened → accepted/declined/expired/countered + decline reasons via Item 87.b). Build the analytics surface: tender-funnel conversion rate by carrier / lane / equipment / day-of-week / hour-of-day; decline reason distribution by carrier tier + lane; AE expiry-preset effectiveness (4h vs 24h vs 48h acceptance rate). **Sprint shape:** Analytics dashboard under `/admin/analytics` (new tab or extension of existing). ~150 LOC across charts + aggregation queries. Sub-rule c gates: Pattern 7 design-system conformance audit (analytics surface across drawer + chart conventions), Sub-pattern 5 audit-both-ends for any new aggregation queries. **Sprint 53+ post-volume.** Requires meaningful tender volume (50+ tenders per week minimum) to produce statistically-useful signal — defer until BKN-onward operational baseline established.

156. ~~**Carrier route RSC payload regression.**~~ **CLOSED 2026-05-17 in v3.8.abx** (Sprint 52.hotfix.a) — **then REOPENED in v3.8.aby** (Sprint 52.hotfix.a.b rollback per Item 157). The explicit `.html` rewrites resolved the Gmail iOS RSC payload issue but surfaced a latent redirect loop on `/carrier/dashboard` (ERR_TOO_MANY_REDIRECTS post-login). Rollback prioritized known-working state; combined fix queued for Sprint 52.hotfix.c after redirect-loop diagnosis. Pre-fix root cause notes preserved: `_redirects` rule `/carrier/* /carrier/:splat 200` echoes `:splat` as identity rewrite target; Cloudflare Pages resolves the extensionless path ambiguously between `out/carrier/<name>.html` and `out/carrier/<name>.txt` siblings (Next.js static export generates both). Gmail iOS WebView Accept-header content negotiation lands on the `.txt` RSC payload. **Status: OPEN (Sprint 52.hotfix.c candidate, combined fix with Item 157).**

157. ~~**Sprint 52.hotfix.a rollback — /carrier/dashboard ERR_TOO_MANY_REDIRECTS.**~~ **CLOSED 2026-05-17 in v3.8.aby** (Sprint 52.hotfix.a.b). Sprint 52.hotfix.a replaced the `/carrier/* /carrier/:splat 200` catch-all with 5 explicit `.html` rewrites for Next.js carrier routes. Production post-deploy verification surfaced a latent redirect loop: INTEGRITY EXPRESS carrier completed login successfully then `/carrier/dashboard` returned ERR_TOO_MANY_REDIRECTS. The redirect loop is presumed to be in the carrier dashboard's auth gate (client-side useCarrierAuth hook OR layout-level redirect), interacting with the new `.html` explicit rewrite in a way the `:splat` echo didn't surface. **Rollback fix:** reverted `_redirects` line 22 to the original `/carrier/* /carrier/:splat 200`. Restores known-working /carrier/dashboard behavior at the cost of reintroducing the Gmail iOS RSC payload regression (Item 156 re-opened). Combined fix planned for Sprint 52.hotfix.c after Phase A diagnostic on BOTH issues — likely involves either (a) auditing the carrier dashboard auth-redirect path for the loop trigger, (b) adopting a hybrid `_redirects` pattern that adds `.html` rewrite for /carrier/login + /carrier/forgot-password + /carrier/reset-password (where the RSC issue surfaced) while leaving `/carrier/dashboard/*` under the `:splat` echo until the auth loop is diagnosed, OR (c) deeper Next.js static export config / middleware investigation.

158. **Parallel carrier status-update endpoints consolidation.** Surfaced 2026-05-17 during Sprint 52.hotfix.c Phase A audit. Two parallel carrier-side status-update routes exist in the codebase: (a) `POST /api/carrier-loads/:id/status` at [`carrierLoads.ts:341`](backend/src/routes/carrierLoads.ts#L341) — what the carrier portal `/my-loads` page actually calls (controller inline, no auditLog wrapper, no central transition validator); (b) `PATCH /api/loads/:id/carrier-status` at [`loads.ts:39`](backend/src/routes/loads.ts#L39) — separate controller `carrierUpdateStatus`, separate validator `updateLoadStatusSchema`, `auditLog("UPDATE_STATUS", "Load")` wrapper. Both gate on `authorize("CARRIER")`. Frontend calls only endpoint (a); endpoint (b) is dead surface with no frontend caller. Same parallel-endpoints class as Sprint 52.hotfix.b Item 156 diagnostic (`/carrier-tenders/active` vs `/api/carrier/tenders`). **Sprint shape:** consolidate to one endpoint; recommend keeping the PATCH variant in loads.ts (auditLog wrapper, REST-correct HTTP verb, validator already separated) and migrating the carrier portal call site. ~30-50 LOC across 3 files (loads.ts unchanged, carrierLoads.ts:335-409 deleted, frontend my-loads page mutation URL + method updated). **Sprint 53+ candidate** — not BKN-blocking; current endpoint A works, just structurally redundant.

159. **Central LoadStatus state-machine validator.** Surfaced 2026-05-17 during Sprint 52.hotfix.c Phase A audit. 13+ distinct write sites mutate `Load.status` across the codebase (tenderController × 4, loadController × 5, carrierLoads.ts, loads.ts/carrierUpdateStatus, documentController, checkCallController, customerController, rateConfirmationController) with NO central transition rules. Each write site accepts whatever status its caller specifies. The `LoadStatus` enum has 18 values across the lifecycle pipeline (DRAFT → POSTED → TENDERED → BOOKED → DISPATCHED → AT_PICKUP → LOADED → IN_TRANSIT → AT_DELIVERY → DELIVERED → POD_RECEIVED → INVOICED → COMPLETED + TONU/CANCELLED/PICKED_UP legacy alias); CLAUDE.md §A.1 documents the canonical state machine but it lives in docs, not code. Carrier portal frontend has a `statusTransitions` map at [`my-loads/page.tsx:12-19`](frontend/src/app/carrier/dashboard/my-loads/page.tsx#L12) that enforces transitions client-side only — backend accepts any of 5 enum values regardless of current status. **Sprint shape:** central `validateLoadStatusTransition(from, to, actor)` helper at `backend/src/lib/loadStateMachine.ts` returning `{ allowed: boolean, reason?: string }`; refactor 13 write sites to invoke validator before `prisma.load.update`; auditLog rejected transitions. ~150-250 LOC across 1 new file + 8 callers (some controllers have multiple write sites). **Sprint 53+ multi-day epic** — significant refactor; gates on Sprint 52 epic completion. Methodology benefit: backend becomes authoritative on transition legality, frontend `statusTransitions` map becomes UI-hint only (not the only enforcement).

160. **ShipmentStatus ↔ LoadStatus enum gap.** Surfaced 2026-05-17 during Sprint 52.hotfix.c Phase A audit. `enum ShipmentStatus` (schema.prisma:197-206) has 8 values: PENDING, BOOKED, DISPATCHED, PICKED_UP, IN_TRANSIT, DELIVERED, COMPLETED, CANCELLED. `enum LoadStatus` (schema.prisma:26-45) has 18 values including the carrier-side states the ShipmentStatus enum LACKS: AT_PICKUP, LOADED, AT_DELIVERY, POD_RECEIVED, INVOICED, TONU. acceptTender at [`tenderController.ts:106`](backend/src/controllers/tenderController.ts#L106) auto-creates a Shipment with `status: "BOOKED"` (line 110) — that value DOES exist in both enums. But if any future flow reads Load.status and writes that value to Shipment.status, the 6 LoadStatus values absent from ShipmentStatus would fail Prisma validation. **Risk profile:** latent — no current code path writes LoadStatus values directly to Shipment.status (acceptTender hardcodes "BOOKED"); future refactor or feature add could trip this gap. **Sprint shape:** decide canonical: (α) expand ShipmentStatus to mirror full LoadStatus pipeline (Shipment becomes a status-tracking projection of Load), (β) keep ShipmentStatus narrow as billing/financial-cycle states only and document that Load.status is the operational source of truth, (γ) drop the Shipment model entirely if it's redundant with Load. Pairs naturally with Item 159 (central state machine) — the enum gap is the data-side expression of the same architectural ambiguity. **Sprint 53+ architectural decision sprint** — requires product call on what Shipment.status represents semantically.

161. **REOPENED + CLOSED 2026-05-17 in v3.8.aca (Sprint 53) — Auth cookie isolation. Original "no bug" close was premature. Sprint 53.a (v3.8.acb) hotfix follow-up — substring-match prefix collision.** Sprint 53 shipped with a substring `.includes("/carrier")` match in `resolveCookieToken` at `middleware/auth.ts:90` that wrongly routed AE-side endpoints with "carrier" in the name to the carrier cookie. Wasi's post-deploy smoke surfaced 403 on `GET /api/carriers` — same architectural class as Sprint 53's parent bug (substring vs proper prefix matching), just at a different layer. **V2 audit** during the Sprint 53.a hotfix enumerated `/api/carrier` (singular) as a genuine audience-mixed mount (6 carrier-facing endpoints `dashboard|scorecard|revenue|bonuses|onboarding-status|documents` lacking explicit `authorize("CARRIER")` + 6 AE-side endpoints `all|:id/detail|:id|verify/:id|admin-setup|capacity-feed` with explicit `authorize("ADMIN", "CEO", ...)`). Single-axis allow-list can't resolve both audiences without one side breaking in the dual-portal scenario. **Decision locked Option B per Wasi 2026-05-17:** allow-list EXCLUDES `/api/carrier` (singular) — the 6 carrier-facing endpoints under it return AE-scoped data when both portals are logged in same browser. Real-world users hold one role per browser so the fallback chain rescues; only deploy-test scenarios hit this. Architectural fix (split mount to move 6 AE-side endpoints into existing `/api/carriers` plural which has overlapping `getAllCarriers` controller anyway, OR introduce X-Portal request header from frontend) tracked as **Sprint 54+ candidate** — same priority as Item 158 (parallel-endpoint consolidation), same class. **Sprint 53.a fix shape:** explicit `CARRIER_PORTAL_MOUNTS` array (`/api/carrier-auth`, `/api/carrier-loads`, `/api/carrier-compliance`, `/api/carrier-payments`, `/api/carrier-tenders`) + `SHIPPER_PORTAL_MOUNTS` array (`/api/shipper-portal`) + new `matchesPortalMount(baseUrl, mounts)` helper using `baseUrl === p || baseUrl.startsWith(p + "/")`. ~25 LOC net change in single file. **Sub-pattern observation gains a second fire:** Sprint 52.hotfix.c missed the cookie layer entirely (Sprint 53 fire #1); Sprint 53 missed the substring-vs-prefix distinction within the cookie layer (fire #2 — same root cause class, one level deeper). The methodology principle banked at Item 161's first close ("Phase A on auth/permission symptoms must reach the storage/transport layer") needs an extension: *"and the prefix-vs-substring distinction within transport-layer routing logic is a hot edge — verify by enumerating ALL mount paths containing the keyword, not by trusting heuristic boundary matching."* Two fires; one more from a future independent incident promotes the principle to §19 canonical per sub-rule c three-fire convention. Sprint 53.a closes 53's regression; original Sprint 53 closure of items 9/10/11/14 remains in force.

 Sprint 52.hotfix.c attributed the carrier "Insufficient permissions" + three-surface status divergence to *observer-identity-confusion* (operator with multi-role privileges polluting their own test session). **Corrected RCA:** all three portals (AE Console, Carrier Portal, Shipper Portal) shared a single httpOnly cookie name `srl_token` set by `backend/src/utils/cookies.ts:14`. Same browser logging into two roles overwrote the cookie — second login replaced the first's JWT. `authorize("CARRIER")` at `backend/src/middleware/auth.ts:165` fired "Insufficient permissions" when the carrier-portal call ran with the ADMIN JWT that had just overwritten the carrier one. The system_log entries Sprint 52.hotfix.c surfaced (`whaider@silkroutelogistics.ai` denied on carrier endpoints) were the contamination *trail*, not test apparatus error. The "test from incognito" workaround masked the bug because incognito has no other portal's cookie to overwrite the carrier one. **Fix shipped Sprint 53:** per-portal cookie names (`srl_token_ae` / `srl_token_carrier` / `srl_token_shipper`), middleware picks the right cookie by `req.baseUrl` prefix, role passed to `setTokenCookie(res, token, role)` at all 14 callsites (authController.ts × 7, routes/auth.ts × 2, carrierAuth.ts × 5), legacy `srl_token` read as one-deploy migration fallback and cleared on next logout. Closes user punch-list items 9 (mark-delivered "Insufficient permissions"), 10 (carrier account auto-switched mid-test), 11 (carrier signout logged out AE). Bundled with Item 14 closure (loginLimiter bumped 5→20 in routes/auth.ts + routes/carrierAuth.ts, authLimiter bumped 30→100 in server.ts — Wasi's lockout during the lifecycle test). **Methodology observation banked as sub-pattern candidate (awaits 3-fire validation per §19 canonical promotion convention):** *"Phase A on auth/permission symptoms must reach the storage/transport layer (cookies, sessions, tokens, headers), not stop at the role gate."* Sprint 52.hotfix.c's Phase A inspected User.role bytes, system_logs, and Neon DB state — but stopped before the cookie layer that delivered the JWT. The "observer-identity-confusion" interpretation was internally consistent with what Phase A surfaced; the gap was scope, not reasoning. Extends Sub-pattern 5 (audit-both-ends-of-data-flow) from data flow to transport flow. Fire #1 banked here. Original "no bug" close preserved below for history.

161-original. ~~**Sprint 52.hotfix.c closed — no bug (observer-identity confusion fire #1).**~~ **CLOSED 2026-05-17 (chore, no version bump, no code change).** Reported symptom was carrier "Update Status: AT PICKUP" button returning "Insufficient permissions" + three-surface status divergence across carrier portal / AE Load Board row / AE Load Board detail panel. Phase A R1-R5 audit + Wasi-side Neon verification confirmed system working as designed: User.role = "CARRIER" byte-exact (length 7, hex `43415252494552`), system_logs healthy (65 SECURITY warnings in past 7 days, latest write <1 minute old at audit time), all recent `authorize()` denials attributed to `whaider@silkroutelogistics.ai` (ADMIN role) attempting carrier-portal endpoints — those denials were CORRECT per the role gate. INTEGRITY EXPRESS session itself was never the denied actor; the symptom surfaced from **cross-role cache contamination from admin's testing session** (admin had AE token in browser storage while testing carrier flows in same tab/window). The three-surface status divergence dissolved when the test was re-run from an incognito window with carrier credentials only — confirming the divergence was browser-state pollution, not data drift. **Methodology observation (fire #1):** *observer-identity-confusion antipattern* — when an operator with multi-role privileges tests a role-restricted flow without isolating session context, observed "bug" may be the test apparatus, not the system. Mitigation: always test role-restricted flows from incognito or separate browser profile with test-subject credentials only. Worth banking for second/third fire validation before promoting to §19 canonical (parallel to sub-pattern 13 + sub-pattern 15 three-fire lineage convention). Sprint 52.hotfix.c closes with zero source change, zero data fix; the Phase A audit work IS the deliverable — Items 158/159/160 banked as collateral findings.

Likely small fix (~30-50 LOC) if regression is purely consumer-side; ~80-120 LOC if ETA compute endpoint also needs hardening. **Related:** Item 159 (Load.status state machine — same write-many-no-validation class as the GPS source field), sub-pattern 5 (audit-both-ends-of-data-flow). **Sprint timing:** post-Sprint-52 epic completion, or interleaved if it surfaces operational friction on the BKN onboarding walkthrough.

180. **Order Builder polish cluster — 11 small UX/operational fixes (umbrella).** Banked 2026-05-20 from Wasi's Sprint 59.c walk-through Q&A. Each sub-item is small (10-80 LOC), single-commit eligible, and not BKN-blocking on its own. Banked as an umbrella so they can be sequenced together when the polish budget opens. None depend on each other; can ship in any order.

   **180.1 — "Duplicate this order" action.** AE running repeat lanes (e.g. weekly BKN Detroit → Chicago) re-keys 30+ fields per draft. Add a one-click clone button on the drafts banner card + per-order kebab menu on the drafts list (Item 179) that creates a new draft with all fields except `id`, `orderNumber`, `loadId`, `status` copied from the source. ~30 LOC.

   **180.2 — Save-as-template for recurring lanes.** Different from 180.1 (template is named + reusable indefinitely; clone is one-shot). Schema addition: new `OrderTemplate` model with `customerId`, `name`, `formData` JSON. New `Template` selector in Section 1 of Order Builder beside Customer picker. AE picks "BKN — Detroit→Chicago weekly" → form prefills from template. Save current draft as new template via "Save as template…" action. ~120-180 LOC + 1 migration.

   **180.3 — Three text-field confusion (specialInstructions / driverInstructions / internalNotes).** Three textareas stacked vertically with similar UI invite AE error (carrier-sensitive info typed into wrong field, or AE-only context where carrier will see it). Single textarea with "visible to" radio (Carrier on rate-con / Driver on rate-con / Internal only) would be cleaner. Backend keeps the 3 columns; frontend collapses to one input + a visibility selector that writes to the corresponding field. ~50 LOC frontend.

   **180.4 — Customer-facing quote approve magic link.** Send quote today emails the customer with the price; customer replies by email; AE manually flips `Order.status = "quote_approved"` (or skips entirely). Add a signed token in the quote email body → public `/quote/approve/<token>` page → customer clicks "Approve at $X,XXX" → backend verifies token + sets `status = "quote_approved"` + emails AE confirmation. Same JWT shape as the magic-link tender accept proposed for Sprint 52b (Item 142). Tightens the quote loop. ~80-120 LOC.

   **180.5 — Quote preview before send.** AE can't see what customer will see before clicking Send quote — risk of typo/rate-error reaching the inbox. Add "Preview email" modal that renders the actual email HTML (calling the same builder used by `sendQuote` controller). Same modal pattern as the RC PDF preview. ~50 LOC.

   **180.6 — Accessorial picker with per-customer negotiated rates.** Current accessorial entry is type + amount + payer (free-form). No connection to customer contract rates. When AE picks "Detention" for BKN, should auto-fill $50/hr (BKN's negotiated rate) vs Acme's $75/hr. Backend has `customer.contractRates` JSON or similar (verify in Phase A). Frontend reads customer's accessorial rates on customer-select and offers them as picker options. ~60-100 LOC.

   **180.7 — Margin-floor alert in OrderSidebar.** OrderSidebar surfaces margin % in real-time. Doesn't appear to alert when target cost produces margin below a configured floor. Add red warning chip when `margin < settings.minMarginPercent` (per-customer override possible). Settings live in `settings` page or `customer.minMarginPercent` column. ~30-50 LOC + maybe 1 schema field.

   **180.8 — `?resume=<orderId>` URL deep-link.** Item 179's drafts page needs URL-shareable resume paths. Today the drafts banner uses internal state mutation (`resumeDraft(d.id)`) with no URL change — AE can't paste a draft link into Slack/email. Add `useEffect` reading `searchParams.get("resume")` on mount; if present, fire `resumeDraft(orderId)`. ~10 LOC. Pairs with Item 179.

   **180.9 — Autosave indicator mirrored near footer CTAs.** Sprint 59.c kept DraftStatus in top header. AE working at the bottom of the form doesn't see it while clicking Tender/Waterfall/Load Board/DAT. Mirror a smaller `<DraftStatus>` chip inside the new footer button row (left side, before the dispatch buttons). ~5 LOC.

   **180.10 — Dispatch error banner relocated to footer.** Sprint 59.b's dispatch error banner renders after the top header but BEFORE the form columns. When dispatch fails from the footer Sprint 59.c moved them to, AE has to scroll back to the top to see the error. Move the banner to be a sibling of the footer button row (rendered above the buttons when isError, below when at very bottom of form). ~10 LOC re-parent.

   **180.11 — Origin/Destination facility name + address visual hierarchy.** Today Section 1 (Origin) + Section 2 (Destination) display fields flat — facility-picker result and address inputs all render at the same visual weight. Wasi 2026-05-20: facility NAME should be the prominent label at the top of each section ("QCC Distribution Center" in larger/bolder type), then address ("1234 Industrial Pkwy, San Diego, CA 92154") as secondary text below. Mirrors the canonical "name primary, supporting metadata below" pattern from CRM customer detail + Carrier Engagement Drawer's selected-carrier card ([CarrierEngagementDrawer.tsx:608-628](frontend/src/components/drawer/CarrierEngagementDrawer.tsx#L608-L628) for reference shape). Apply to both origin + destination sections. Address fields stay editable for AE override when facility lookup misses or a one-off address is needed. ~40-60 LOC across both sections (FacilityPicker result rendering + section header restructure).

177. **Visual-verification protocol gate — mandatory for drawer/modal/canvas-rendering sprints.** Banked 2026-05-18 alongside Sprint 59.a (v3.8.acn) hotfix closure. **Codified per Wasi ratification 2026-05-18.** Pre-Sprint-59.a state: pre-commit gates were `tsc --noEmit` + `next build` (Sub-pattern 11 CI-parity canonical). Sprint 59 shipped with both gates green but missed 4 user-facing UX bugs (horizontal tabs vs vertical IconTabs canonical, empty form on open, carrier name mismatch, customer rate duplication) — all compile-time clean, none caught by tsc or build. **Sub-pattern 8 (conditional-render-visual-verification) fired again** — second instance in this session arc (first was Sprint 48.c signature overlap at Item 139 canonical). Protocol mandate: **any sprint that ships a new drawer, modal, canvas-rendered surface, or visual layout restructure MUST include a pre-push visual smoke** — either via Playwright headed-browser screenshot (when CI-feasible) OR explicit Phase A code-trace of the visual class structure against the canonical reference, NOT just function signatures. Sub-pattern 8 sub-rule a: *"code-trace must include the visual-outcome class chain, not just the call graph."* Sub-pattern 8 sub-rule b: *"every new drawer surface re-verifies against the canonical right-drawer reference (currently T&T LoadDetailDrawer at [LoadDetailDrawer.tsx:108-112](frontend/src/app/dashboard/track-trace/LoadDetailDrawer.tsx#L108)) — IconTabs left strip + flex-1 main content sibling — NOT inline horizontal tabs in the form body."* Future Phase A audits checking drawer canonical must trace BOTH the component file's tab pattern (already done at Sprint 59 A3) AND the wrapping flex direction (`flex` vs `flex-col`) AND the sibling structure (`<IconTabs />` as first child, then `<div className="flex-1 flex flex-col min-w-0">`). Single-axis component-file audit produced the Sprint 59 miss. **Sprint shape for future drawer work:** Phase A canonical-trace adds step "A_visual" — read the canonical drawer's outermost JSX wrapper class chain + first 3 child siblings, document the visual hierarchy in the report, and confirm Phase B implementation matches. Costs ~10 minutes per Phase A; saves the kind of post-deploy hotfix that Sprint 59.a was. Item 177 closes structurally — the protocol is canonical from this commit forward, not a pending implementation. Pairs with Sub-pattern 11 (CI-parity) — together they form a two-gate pre-push discipline (compile gate + visual gate) for any UX-shipping sprint.

167. ~~**Order Builder direct-tender silent failure.**~~ **CLOSED STRUCTURALLY 2026-05-18 in v3.8.acj** (Sprint 59). 175. **RSC payload 404 on root `/index.txt?_rsc=*` requests.** Banked 2026-05-18 during Sprint 174.a (v3.8.ach) hotfix audit. Symptom in Wasi's DevTools console: `/index.txt?_rsc=1ri1u: Failed to load resource: the server responded with a status of 404`. Same architectural class as §13.3 Item 156 (carrier route RSC payload — Gmail iOS WebView Accept-header content negotiation) but on the root path rather than `/carrier/*`. Cloudflare Pages doesn't have an `/index.txt` static file because Next.js static export generates `/index.html` only; the `?_rsc=*` query string is a Next.js App Router internal RSC (React Server Components) payload fetch attempt. Static export shouldn't be emitting RSC fetches at all, but framework versions occasionally regress on this. **Sprint shape:** investigate which component or framework version is emitting the RSC fetch. Options: (a) check `frontend/next.config.ts` for any RSC-enabling config that conflicts with `output: "export"`; (b) audit framework version + Next.js patch notes for RSC-in-static-export regressions; (c) add `_redirects` rule `/index.txt /index.html 200` as a band-aid that satisfies the fetch with the actual page content. Low priority — RSC payload fetch failures don't break the page render (Next.js gracefully falls back to client-side navigation), they just produce console noise. Pairs with Item 156 architecturally (same RSC content-negotiation class). Sprint slot: post-BKN cleanup unless a user-facing symptom surfaces.

174. ~~**Shipper login role-gate gap — carrier creds work on /shipper/login.**~~ **CLOSED 2026-05-18 in v3.8.acf** (Sprint Item 174, Option β+γ+α defense-in-depth). Symptom: INTEGRITY EXPRESS (aliabbas6361@gmail.com, role=CARRIER) could complete /shipper/login → OTP → land on /shipper/dashboard authenticated, despite being a carrier account. Shipper API gates (`authorize("SHIPPER")`) held so no data leak, but portal-boundary integrity violated. **Three-layer gap audited:** (a) shipper login page reuses AE auth endpoints — [shipper/login/page.tsx:10,46](frontend/src/app/shipper/login/page.tsx#L10) imports `useAuthStore` calling `/api/auth/login` + `/api/auth/verify-otp` (the AE endpoints, not separate shipper paths); (b) `/api/auth/login` at [authController.ts:148-218](backend/src/controllers/authController.ts#L148) had no role gate — only password + lockout + isActive checks; (c) `/api/auth/verify-otp` had SHIPPER-specific `checkShipperApproval` but no refusal for non-SHIPPER roles — carrier flowed straight through to JWT issuance; (d) shipper dashboard layout at [shipper/dashboard/layout.tsx:48-61](frontend/src/app/shipper/dashboard/layout.tsx#L48) had no role check — only `if (!currentUser)`. **Fix shape — defense-in-depth at three layers (Option β+γ+α combined):** Layer γ-1 backend validator: optional `expectedRole: "AE" | "SHIPPER"` added to `loginSchema` ([validators/auth.ts](backend/src/validators/auth.ts)) + `otpSchema` ([routes/auth.ts:23](backend/src/routes/auth.ts#L23)). Layer γ-2 backend controller: new `AE_ROLES` set + `rolesMatch(userRole, expectedRole)` helper at [authController.ts:21-30](backend/src/controllers/authController.ts#L21); role check in `login` after isActive check + in `handleVerifyOtp` after user lookup. 401 + `code: "ROLE_MISMATCH"`, message "Invalid credentials for this portal." Layer γ-3 useAuthStore: `login` + `verifyOtp` signatures extended with optional `expectedRole`, body conditionally includes the field. Layer β shipper login: passes `"SHIPPER"` to both calls; post-OTP frontend role check (defense-in-depth in case backend gate fails) — on mismatch calls `/api/auth/logout` + `useAuthStore.getState().clearAuth()` + shows error. Layer γ-4 AE login: passes `"AE"` in both fetch bodies (page uses raw fetch, not useAuthStore). Layer α shipper dashboard layout: `bounceIfWrongRole` helper called from both fresh-load and cached-user branches — on mismatch calls `/api/auth/logout` + clearAuth + `router.replace("/shipper/login")`. **Carrier portal unaffected** — uses `/api/carrier-auth/*` which already gates strictly to CARRIER role per [carrierAuth.ts:70](backend/src/routes/carrierAuth.ts#L70) + [carrierAuth.ts:153](backend/src/routes/carrierAuth.ts#L153). **Methodology — sub-pattern fire #1 banked: "portal-boundary-defense-asymmetry":** *"When one portal (carrier) has rigorous role gating across login/OTP/layout but another (shipper) reuses shared AE auth endpoints without role gates, the asymmetry becomes a portal-boundary violation surface. Audit all three portals' login flows for symmetric defense at each layer."* Sub-pattern awaits fire #2 + #3 from independent incidents before §19 canonical promotion. Pairs with Item 168 (audit-wrong-code-path) and Item 169 (interceptor-without-context-awareness) — three consecutive scope/context-discipline sub-pattern candidates banked in the Sprint 53→54→174 arc.

Sprint 54 portal-aware 401 interceptor routes carrier-dashboard 401s to /carrier/login correctly. **Wasi's re-test on May 18 in fresh incognito confirmed no kick-out — carrier login works end-to-end.** The original symptom was dual-portal cookie contamination from yesterday's test session (AE cookie present in the same browser polluting carrier endpoint resolution); Sprint 53.a CARRIER_PORTAL_MOUNTS preferred-cookie selection resolves this when the request lands on a carrier-portal mount with srl_token_carrier present. Fresh-incognito sessions don't have AE cookie contamination, so the fix surfaces cleanly. **No source change for Item 168** — closure is a posture correction: this was a Sprint 53.a downstream resolution, not a separate Sprint-needing bug. Yesterday's "audit-wrong-code-path" sub-pattern fire #1 stands — banking remains valid even though the underlying bug self-resolved, because the methodology miss (auditing AE flow instead of carrier flow) was real regardless.

Carrier auth lives at `backend/src/routes/carrierAuth.ts` with its own `handleVerifyOtp` and totp-verify handlers, separate `useCarrierAuth` Zustand store, separate `/carrier/login` UI. Sub-pattern banks alongside Sprint 53 + 53.a fires #1 (cookie layer scope) + #2 (substring-vs-prefix within cookie layer); cumulative pattern: Phase A scope-discipline failures cluster around "what was the user actually testing?" rather than "where does the code think it lives?". Sub-pattern awaits fire #2 + #3 from independent incidents before §19 canonical promotion per sub-rule c three-fire convention.

169. **HTTP interceptor-without-context-awareness (sub-pattern candidate fire #1).** Banked 2026-05-17 alongside Sprint 54 close of Item 6 (View Tender CTA wrong portal). The frontend axios 401 interceptor at `frontend/src/lib/api.ts:35-42` (pre-Sprint-54) made a portal-routing decision (`/auth/login` redirect target) based only on the response status code, with no reference to `window.location.pathname` to know which portal the request originated from. Net effect: a logged-out carrier landing on `/carrier/dashboard/tenders` from an email CTA got bounced to the AE login page on first 401, despite the carrier portal having its own `/carrier/login` surface. Sprint 54 fixed by reading `window.location.pathname` and picking `/carrier/login` / `/shipper/login` / `/auth/login` accordingly. **Methodology lesson banked as Sub-rule c sub-pattern candidate fire #1 — "interceptor-without-context-awareness":** *"Frontend HTTP interceptors that make routing decisions on responses (e.g. 401 → redirect) must read request context (URL path, expected portal) before deciding the target. Hardcoded fallbacks erase user origin context."* Candidate awaits fire #2 + #3 from independent incidents before §19 canonical promotion. Pairs with Items 168 + Sprint 53 audit-wrong-code-path lineage — both point to the same broader meta-pattern: scope/context discipline in audit AND in code design. **Cross-reference:** Item 168 (audit-wrong-code-path, methodology); this Item 169 (interceptor-without-context, code-design). Different layers, same shape.

170. **Carrier portal Rate Confirmation download visibility (Sprint Phase 2 follow-on).** Banked 2026-05-17 alongside Sprint Phase 2 close (auto-RC on tender accept, v3.8.acd). Phase 2 produces auto-DRAFT RCs on tender accept and AE manually sends them via existing `POST /api/rate-confirmations/:id/send` (email + PDF attachment to carrier). What's STILL missing: a carrier-portal endpoint that exposes RC download by loadId — `GET /api/rate-confirmations/:id/pdf` is CARRIER-authorized but requires the RC's UUID which the carrier doesn't have. `GET /api/rate-confirmations/load/:loadId` lookup is AE-only (carrier role not in authorize list at `backend/src/routes/rateConfirmations.ts:20`). **Sprint shape:** (a) new endpoint `GET /api/rate-confirmations/load/:loadId/latest/pdf` (CARRIER authorized, verifies carrier owns the load, looks up most recent RC, streams PDF via existing `generateEnhancedRateConfirmation`) — returns 404 if no RC exists yet; (b) add CARRIER to `GET /api/rate-confirmations/load/:loadId` authorize list for metadata reads (status, sentAt, signed flag) so the carrier UI can gate the download button correctly; (c) frontend `/carrier/dashboard/my-loads` load detail panel — replace `rateConfirmationPdfUrl` column gating with TanStack query against the new endpoint, "Download Rate Confirmation" button always visible for BOOKED+ status with disabled "pending" state when no RC exists. ~50 LOC across 2 files backend + 1 file frontend. **Priority:** queue after Phase 2 deploy soak — carriers currently receive RC via email attachment so Phase 2 is functionally complete without this; portal download is a re-download convenience. Pairs with Item 171 (auto-send) — if 171 ships first, this becomes more relevant. **Sprint slot:** post-Sprint-54 carrier-OTP audit (Item 168), interleave before Sprint 56 if BKN onboarding asks for re-download UX.

171. **Auto-send the RC on tender accept (Sprint Phase 2.b follow-on).** Banked 2026-05-17 alongside Sprint Phase 2 close. AE still gets the notification with deep-link, but the RC is also already in the carrier's inbox within seconds of accept. **Risks:** wrong-data RC in carrier's inbox is recoverable (AE re-sends after fix) but damages trust on early loads. **Trigger conditions for elevation:** auto-fill mapping has been smoke-verified over at least 3 real test loads with no field corrections needed; BKN onboarding asks for industry-standard auto-send timing. ~30 LOC: per-customer or env-gate read inside acceptTender + acceptTenderOnBehalf, fires `sendRateConfirmation` controller's internals after auto-RC create.
